  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_99de6486-afb8-4ca1-a34e-f26e82f23fb9'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

Yet Rachel's feisty spirit might just be heaven-sent to save a tough, stubborn man.<br /><br />Dare To Dream<br /><br />Welcome to Salvation, North Carolina—where a man who's forgotten what tenderness means meets a woman with nothing to lose. here two endearing lovers will set off on a funny, touching journey of the heart. . .to a place where dreams just might come true.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15105446613449529280"><b>5 FAT Stars!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475081604ra/20679146.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I basically stepped on a landmine here. You see, I’m scared of books where the hero is pining after his ex. But a dead ex AND a dead child? A <i>nightmare</i>.<br/><br/>After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73080.Nobody_s_Baby_But_Mine__Chicago_Stars___3_' title='Nobody's Baby But Mine (Chicago Stars, #3) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nobody's Baby But Mine</a> I just one-clicked this one and dove in. It turns out it’s a good thing I didn’t read the blurb. Had I read it, I wouldn’t have discovered this outstanding book. Not only did the subject matter NOT bother me at all, but it actually <i>blew me away</i>.<br/><br/>I won’t say more about this book except for two thing</span>
  <span id="freeText15105446613449529280" style="display:none"><b>5 FAT Stars!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475081604ra/20679146.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I basically stepped on a landmine here. You see, I’m scared of books where the hero is pining after his ex. But a dead ex AND a dead child? A <i>nightmare</i>.<br><br>After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73080.Nobody_s_Baby_But_Mine__Chicago_Stars___3_" title="Nobody's Baby But Mine (Chicago Stars, #3) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Nobody's Baby But Mine</a> I just one-clicked this one and dove in. It turns out it’s a good thing I didn’t read the blurb. Had I read it, I wouldn’t have discovered this outstanding book. Not only did the subject matter NOT bother me at all, but it actually <i>blew me away</i>.<br><br>I won’t say more about this book except for two things:<br><br>1. I loved every word and adored every character: Gabe’s assholeness and crankiness, Rachel’s free spirit, optimism and strength (even her ridiculous oxfords and ugly housedresses), Edward’s innocence and fragileness, Ethan’s ignorance, Kristy’s shyness and lack of confidence, Jane’s genius, Cal’s impulsiveness and Rosie’s cuteness.<br><br>2. It took me longer than usual to read this book but not for the reasons you might think. Let’s just say that reading this book can be compared to eating the world’s finest chocolate cake. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475081604ra/20679147.gif" height="100" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475081604ra/20679148.gif" width="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Imagine that you are enjoying a <s>chocolate cake</s> book so much that you don't want it to ever end. To your horror, you suddenly realize it will soon be over... <br><br>What do you do?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475081604ra/20679155.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475081604ra/20679149.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>You decide to <s>eat</s> read only <s>a piece</s> forty pages or so a day so that you can savor each <s>piece</s> word slowly and possessively and prolong the enjoyment for as long as possible.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475081604ra/20679150.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475081604ra/20679151.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475081604ra/20679153.gif" height="120" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475081604ra/20679152.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>If you haven’t tried this author yet, I highly recommend doing it soon. I'm ashamed to admit, but I always thought her books were nothing more than cliché and sappy chick lit stories because of their unappealing covers. The truth is, however, Susan Elizabeth Phillips is an amazing character developer and unique story teller.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475081604ra/20679154.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>QUICK REVIEW:</b><br><br><b>Enjoyment:</b>: 5/5<br><b>Writing style:</b> 5/5<br><b>Storyline:</b> 5/5<br><b>Hero:</b> 5/5<br><b>Heroine:</b> 5/5<br><b>Secondary characters:</b> 5/5 <br><b>Hotness/chemistry:</b> 4/5 <br><b>Romance:</b> 5/5 <br><b>Angst:</b> 3/5<br><b>Darkness level:</b> 3/5<br><b>Humor:</b> 4/5<br><b> Depth of the book:</b> 5/5<br><b>POV:</b> multiple, 3rd person<br><b> Triggers:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[death of a spouse and a child <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1510504825i/24426022._SX540_.jpg" width='400"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1236392112" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1236392112" />
    <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon"><img alt="♥Sharon♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417537732p2/12125670.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1236392112?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Sharon♥" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon">♥Sharon♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12125670-sharon?shelf=audible">audible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1236392112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17932811316645642234"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1590281888i/29530497._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>There is no surprise here that I loved this audio book! ❤️ And it is safe to say that I loved listening to it just a bit more than sitting and reading it. The narrator Anna Fields did a fabulous job bringing these characters to life. <br/><br/>My original review is below so I won't go on about the story other than to say it was AMAZING. As were the characters; Rachel Stone, Gabe Bonner and the ever so sweet Edward. ❤️<br/><br/>If you loved reading this series do yourself a favor and listen to a few. You will not be</span>
  <span id="freeText17932811316645642234" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1590281888i/29530497._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>There is no surprise here that I loved this audio book! ❤️ And it is safe to say that I loved listening to it just a bit more than sitting and reading it. The narrator Anna Fields did a fabulous job bringing these characters to life. <br><br>My original review is below so I won't go on about the story other than to say it was AMAZING. As were the characters; Rachel Stone, Gabe Bonner and the ever so sweet Edward. ❤️<br><br>If you loved reading this series do yourself a favor and listen to a few. You will not be disappointed!<br><br>❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️<br>I am finding by reading this series back to back I am running out of creative opening lines for my reviews. So I guess I will go back to the basics. Simply put, I loved this book. I love Susan Elizabeth Phillips writing. I love her creativity. With each one of these books she gives you a little ‘something’ that makes the story special. <br> <br>In <b>Dream a Little Dream</b> that ‘something’ was the sweetest little 5 year old boy who stole my heart within minutes of starting the book. For me Edward was at the heart of this story. He was the precious son of Rachel Stone’s and the little boy that would help mend Gabriel Bonner’s heart.<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/4028597d-509e-4824-8f2e-7f9f442ef8f8_zps5fyak3xd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434329287i/15204979._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 4028597d-509e-4824-8f2e-7f9f442ef8f8_zps5fyak3xd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There was more sadness in this one than in the others. It surrounded Rachel, Gabe and even Edward. But along with the sadness there was hope. There was a bit of humor. And then there was that thread of need and desire.<br><br><b>Rachel Stone~ </b> was a fighter. I loved the beauty within her. Rachel had chosen a life that at the time she thought would make her happy, a life that would be fulfilling. But soon she was stripped of everything. Her ex-husband was a crook, hated by all and she was left fighting for her future and that of her little boy. <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/e0699f7a-d6fe-48af-ba8c-5e3205eaa997_zpsi7sfvfea.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434329287i/15204980._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo e0699f7a-d6fe-48af-ba8c-5e3205eaa997_zpsi7sfvfea.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Gabe Bonner~ </b>had lost all that was precious to him. He had such a sad soul and he was living a life that he truly didn’t care much about. It didn’t matter that he had a caring family. He struggled to get past his heartache.<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/9f81f9b3-3c71-4922-b899-4dca1fcf220c_zpsg8bsspgv.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434329287i/15204981._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 9f81f9b3-3c71-4922-b899-4dca1fcf220c_zpsg8bsspgv.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Things were not easy for both Gabe and Rachel. Both of them had their own struggles. It wasn’t always apparent but each of them was giving the other a little bit of hope. My heart broke for both of them. <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/776024f3-5377-457d-92ae-b496163962ae_zpsobq7jluu.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434329287i/15204982.jpg" alt=" photo 776024f3-5377-457d-92ae-b496163962ae_zpsobq7jluu.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Rachel was the first to realize that in his own way Gabe, was adding a little happiness to her life. But she also had Edward to think about. He was the most important person in her life. His future would always come first.<br><br>And even though something seemed to settle within Gabe he was limited to what he could offer Rachel and Edward. She saw things within him that he wasn’t sure he could change.<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/00dd9b8f-63bf-4a76-bf9b-cdfa07400e90_zpsrnwlze55.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434329287i/15204983._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 00dd9b8f-63bf-4a76-bf9b-cdfa07400e90_zpsrnwlze55.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There is a saying, “Love is patient, Love is kind…….Love never fails. Thank goodness for that. And thank goodness for Edward. He was an angel. <br> <br>This was such a wonderful story. It certainly was one that filled my heart to the brim. And I will steal a line from my sweet friend Karen’s review. “Romance books don’t get any better than this.”<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/xxxx_zpsqhuirhsd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434329493i/15205010.jpg" alt=" photo xxxx_zpsqhuirhsd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17932811316645642234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15316149249657113235">I swear, books in this series are getting better and better. Every next one I start I am like, wow! this is the best! And then I go to the next one and want to say the same thing about it. To be fair I have to say all of them are amazing. I can't believe it took me so long to start reading this series.<br/><br/>It's a classic contemporary romance at its best. The story, characters, angst and all the feels... so wonderful. Everything perfect and so well written. I recommend to all of you who love good love</span>
  <span id="freeText15316149249657113235" style="display:none">I swear, books in this series are getting better and better. Every next one I start I am like, wow! this is the best! And then I go to the next one and want to say the same thing about it. To be fair I have to say all of them are amazing.     <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6972914-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529600203p2/6972914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1221488740?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/6972914-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6972914-karen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1221488740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11601060056725886713"><b>5 STARS</b><br/><span>[image error]</span><a href='http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects%203/25dee057-a325-4e81-902d-1bfd35838aa6.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427414787i/14269550._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo 25dee057-a325-4e81-902d-1bfd35838aa6.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>You know, I keep trying, but I cannot rate any of Susan Elizabeth Phillips’ books less than 5. It just isn’t ever going to happen. And each one I read suddenly becomes my favorite. And this one is no exception. Seriously, these books are FUCKING SENSATIONAL! And that is all I need to say about it. <br/><br/><span>[image error]</span><a href='http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Women%202/1550_image_67990.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427412460i/14269427._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo 1550_image_67990.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>Rachel Stone</b> is only twenty-seven and already the destitute widow of a dead crooked television evangelist. She is a public pariah, who has lost everything, her </span>
  <span id="freeText11601060056725886713" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS</b><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects%203/25dee057-a325-4e81-902d-1bfd35838aa6.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427414787i/14269550._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 25dee057-a325-4e81-902d-1bfd35838aa6.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>You know, I keep trying, but I cannot rate any of Susan Elizabeth Phillips’ books less than 5. It just isn’t ever going to happen. And each one I read suddenly becomes my favorite. And this one is no exception. Seriously, these books are FUCKING SENSATIONAL! And that is all I need to say about it. <br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Women%202/1550_image_67990.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427412460i/14269427._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 1550_image_67990.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Rachel Stone</b> is only twenty-seven and already the destitute widow of a dead crooked television evangelist. She is a public pariah, who has lost everything, her husband, her home, all of her money, her possessions and even her faith in God. All she has left in the world is her sweet but sickly and very sad little five year old boy named Edward. <br><br><b>
  <i>”Everybody hates us.”</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Funny/30d9d4f3441f965547b0e9ca57a817b9.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426196637i/13986649.jpg" alt=" photo 30d9d4f3441f965547b0e9ca57a817b9.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Everywhere she goes she is shunned and denied work. So finally after living out of her car… it finally gives up the ghost back in none other than her own hometown of Salvation, North Carolina. Where everyone REMEMBERS. And everyone HATES her.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Ironic, isn't it, what religion does to people?"<br>"I guess it's more ironic what people do to religion.” </i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Men2/tumblr_mo6ow8xgqq1s7vpd9o1_500.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427412460i/14269428._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo tumblr_mo6ow8xgqq1s7vpd9o1_500.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Then there’s <b>Gabriel Bonner</b>. The long lost <b>brother</b> of Cal Bonner (yes our gorgeous and notorious quarterback for the famous Chicago Stars). Gabe has returned to Salvation after spending a few years in Mexico trying to drink away his grief. He lost his adored wife and son in a horrible car accident a few years back and has yet to recover from their loss. <br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects%203/drive-in-theater.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427412460i/14269429._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo drive-in-theater.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>”What kind of moron opens a drive-in?”</i>
</b><br><br>And he’s given up his practice as the local veterinarian, so he can re-open the long dead drive-in theater. But while pursuing this painful and useless task, he is faced with yet another unpleasant task… turning away the very famous, very hated, and very desperate “Widow Snopes.”<br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects%203/tumblr_kuhu14mPf51qatmbuo1_400.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427412460i/14269430._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo tumblr_kuhu14mPf51qatmbuo1_400.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“Who needs food? Your smile alone is enough to nourish me for weeks.” </i>
</b><br><br>And yes… love is found but not easily. Gabe must first find a way to put his past behind him, and then find a way to trust this snarky, skinny, and tenacious young girl. And even then there is a persistent <i>little</i> problem… named Edward.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects%203/03f82c04-458c-40c0-a99f-47ab19beeb02.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427412460i/14269431._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 03f82c04-458c-40c0-a99f-47ab19beeb02.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>He felt an unfamiliar heat in his chest and knew that his malevolence had begun to char the borders of his heart.</i>
</b><br><br>This book was sooooooo good… that even my updates had several people picking it back up for a re-read. And I know for a fact, that I will be doing the same thing myself very soon. <br><br>Romance books don’t get any better than this. And if they do… I’ll bet SEP is involved somehow. So from here, I’ll give a few quotes and pictures, and then, I’m on to my next favorite in the series! <br><br><b>
  <i>”You’re not people Bonner, I’m not even sure you’re human.”</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Tags/26132-Sometimesyougottapretendev.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427413245i/14269461.jpg" alt=" photo 26132-Sometimesyougottapretendev.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>His chest burned. Her compassion made him defenseless. Just seconds earlier he’d been dreading her waspish tongue, but now he would give anything to be hit by one of her wisecracks.</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects%203/father-son-hug1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427412460i/14269432._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo father-son-hug1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>”Butthead.”</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Funny/Holyheremindedmeofbutthead_b3484ac75b60049c893a2bca6d38b88b.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427412460i/14269433._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo Holyheremindedmeofbutthead_b3484ac75b60049c893a2bca6d38b88b.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>”Cherry was the love of my boyhood, Rach. You’re the love of my manhood. And I do love you, with all my heart. Please don’t leave me.”</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Couples/The-Notebook-11.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427412460i/14269434._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo The-Notebook-11.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18415419540075166587"><i>Written July 9, 2015</i><br/><br/><b>4.7 Stars - Wonderful, touching, lovely .... simply great</b><br/><br/>The last one for me to read in this lovely <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/show/40360-chicago-stars' rel='nofollow noopener'>Chicago Stars</a> series. 11:30 hrs audiobook narrated by the FANTASTIC <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/62817.Anna_Fields' title='Anna Fields' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anna Fields</a>.<br/><br/><a href='http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/><b>Once again; I'm happydancing</b><br/>I'm not exaggerating, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/41313.Susan_Elizabeth_Phillips' title='Susan Elizabeth Phillips' rel='nofollow noopener'>Susan Elizabeth Phillips</a> is still one of the very BEST in this feel good m/f genre. <br/><br/>*********************************************<br/><br/><b><i>Dream a Little Dream</i> from the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/show/40360-chicago-stars' rel='nofollow noopener'>Chicago Stars</a> football 'world' is book #4</b> published 1998 and my sev</span>
  <span id="freeText18415419540075166587" style="display:none"><i>Written July 9, 2015</i><br><br><b>4.7 Stars - Wonderful, touching, lovely .... simply great</b><br><br>The last one for me to read in this lovely <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/show/40360-chicago-stars" rel="nofollow noopener">Chicago Stars</a> series. 11:30 hrs audiobook narrated by the FANTASTIC <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/62817.Anna_Fields" title="Anna Fields" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna Fields</a>.<br><br><a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386992968ra/7500988.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Once again; I'm happydancing</b><br>I'm not exaggerating, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/41313.Susan_Elizabeth_Phillips" title="Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Susan Elizabeth Phillips</a> is still one of the very BEST in this feel good m/f genre. <br><br>*********************************************<br><br><b><i>Dream a Little Dream</i> from the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/show/40360-chicago-stars" rel="nofollow noopener">Chicago Stars</a> football 'world' is book #4</b> published 1998 and my seventh (and last book - not read in order - standalones) in this fantastic series. (See my reviews <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ in my reading order:<br><br>I first <u>read</u> two as paperbacks: <br>• <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/719495741" rel="nofollow noopener">#2 - Heaven, Texas (5 stars)</a></b>,<br>Gracie Snow &amp; Bobby Tom Denton<br>• <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/720099328?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">#1 - It Had to Be You (4.5 stars)</a></b>,<br>Phoebe Somerville &amp; Dan Calebow<br><br>Then I started to listening to the audiobooks. Every one faultlessly narrated by the fantastic <i>Anna Fields</i>: <br>• <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/829947576?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">#7 - Natural Born Charmer (4.1 stars)</a></b>,<br>Blue Bailey &amp; Dean Robillard<br>• <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1054797783?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">#5 - This Heart of Mine (4,0 stars)</a></b>,<br>Molly Somerwille &amp; Kevin Tucker<br>• <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/724261693" rel="nofollow noopener">#3 - Nobody's Baby But Mine (4.7 stars)</a></b>,<br>Jane Darlington &amp; Cal Bonner<br>• <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/913008000?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">#6 - Match Me If You Can (4.4 stars)</a></b>,<br> Annabelle Granger &amp; Heath Champion<br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> ~ All sweet romantic in a well-written very amusing feelgood style. Higly recommended as audiobooks as well.)<br><br>*********************************************<br><br>We are once again back in <i>Salvation, North Carolina</i>, the small mountain town with three goodlooking <i>Bonner</i> brothers. We met the oldest (charmer) in book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/724261693" rel="nofollow noopener">#3 - Nobody's Baby But Mine (4.7 stars)</a> (my favorite part so far). <br><br>In <i>Dream a Little Dream</i> is it time for the middle brother, <b>Gabriel 'Gabe' Bonner</b>. A mourning man who lost his wife and kid in an horrible car accident a couple of years ago. Gabe is back in town and he bought the old drive-in movie and is now trying to make it to it's old shiny glance once again. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436119507i/15421195._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="156" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Our heroine is <b>Rachel Stone</b> a single mother with a lovely five years old boy, the über cute <i>Edward</i> (who wants to be called <i>Chip</i>...), just 10 single bucks in her pockets, old clothes and a broken miserable car. Life sucks!! ~ Rachel returns to Salvation to find her dead husbands disappeared money-treasure (or is there any?). Her husband was a an older popular preacher (very Bible faithful) who in God's &amp; Jesus' name cheated and tricked a lot of believer of their last money and trust in their savior. Not surprisingly are people in town still angry and many hate, the back then diamond-sprinkled, greedy young preacher wife. Nowadays called "Widow Snopes". <br><blockquote>“Ironic, isn't it, what religion does to people?”<br>“I guess it's more ironic what people do to to people.”<br><br><a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Diverse/fc66da38-8bdb-4040-840e-baad7a29c967_zpsopu1g8cs.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436459847i/15462637.jpg" alt=" photo fc66da38-8bdb-4040-840e-baad7a29c967_zpsopu1g8cs.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
</blockquote><br><b>Rachel will do anything to keep her child safe</b> and she need money to give him a better future. Welcome or not, she must stay in Salvation and start her search and she immediately need work. Gabe need a strong hardworking "handyman" and our tough heroine think she is perfect for the job. <br><blockquote>‘He wanted to protect her and fuck her and comfort her and destroy her all at once. The chaos of his emotions coiled around his pain, deepening the agony.’</blockquote><br>...Needy or not, our hero disagrees strongly. A "enemies to lovers" story starts. <br><br>********************************************<br><br><b>An emotional roller coaster..</b><br><i>Dream a Little Dream</i> is maybe the most emotional, sad, angsty and touching heart-wrenching of the books in this 'Chicago Stars' series. This story was about two people which suffers from a terrible past. They are both alone and both Rachel and Gabe are so filled with anger about the past and nearly desperate in their way to build big strong walls against themself. ~ Grandly romantic, steaming hot and addictive good narrated. ..Of course.<br><blockquote>
<a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Diverse/fc66da38-8bdb-4040-840e-baad7a29c967_zpsopu1g8cs.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436459847i/15462637.jpg" alt=" photo fc66da38-8bdb-4040-840e-baad7a29c967_zpsopu1g8cs.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>“Chip, I know you don't understand this, but I'd take it as a personal favor if you'd stop trying to marry your mother off to my brothers.” </blockquote><br>Add a adorable little scared boy. A small tiny pre-school boy who fears death and is so heartbreaking grateful for everything he gets. He dreams about to sit on a fathers big shoulders, be strong and see his mummy happy. I loved this little sweet Chip and <i>Anna Fields</i>, this terrific 'child voice' narrator, did him even more lovely. ~ My eyes filled with tears at times. Sob!! <br><br>*********************************************<br><br>Really fun and amusing was also <b>the second characters own love story</b> (as in every SEP book). It was with Gabe's younger brother, Reverend <i>Ethan Bonner</i> and the "good dear old" (boring nice but invisible) <i>Kristy</i>. The girl who always does "everything" for her dear old childhood love who nearly see her. That's before she decides to change her life a bit and does a needed "makeover". Poor Ethan is shocked (..and shockingly aching stone hard). Oh!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436456909i/15462049._SX540_.png" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Dream a Little Dream</i> is perfect if you love stories with big funny families and razy protective brothers. Stories with cute bright kids and a story set in a small <i>everybody knows everybody</i> town. And most of all if you prefer romances with gorgeous, sulky, insistent and horny alpha males. Add a strong tough heroine. Not kinky or next to erotic porn, but hot and smexy enough. <br><br><b>You knew it will end with a lovely HEA</b> but you still feel that the journey to those three magic words (and the sound of the church bells) is the best part with reading romances. — If that is the kind of books you usually like then are you going to enjoy this one you too.<br><br>*********************************************<br><br><i><a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386992968ra/7500988.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386992968ra/7500988.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386992968ra/7500988.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386992968ra/7500988.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386992968ra/7500988.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> ~ 5 bumping hearts for 7 great books.</i><br><br><b>Seven romances, and this was my last one. Sob!</b><br>I'm so glad I started this series —thanks to Kathleen (..the California Snowman) who recommended me the first one I read and loved, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/719495741" rel="nofollow noopener">#2 - Heaven, Texas (5 stars)</a>. I havn't read these book-parts in any order and it worked fine for me. Just pick one, they are all good. <br><br><b>I LIKE - and I'll miss this fantastic SEP world</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="18415419540075166587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61719857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer740180458926810094">I avoided this book for some reason. Possibly because I wasn't in the mood to read about a non athlete hero after falling through SEP's Chicago Stars. I'm glad I did get around to read it since it is one of the most heartwrenching stories I've read. Chip, Rachel's son, is absolutely adorable. Especially his relationship with Cal's daughter, Rosie. Gabe and Rachel's relationship grew slowly and pain was involved considering their pasts, but in a SEP's manner, they do end up together. Ethan and Kr</span>
  <span id="freeText740180458926810094" style="display:none">I avoided this book for some reason. Possibly because I wasn't in the mood to read about a non athlete hero after falling through SEP's Chicago Stars. I'm glad I did get around to read it since it is one of the most heartwrenching stories I've read. Chip, Rachel's son, is absolutely adorable. Especially his relationship with Cal's daughter, Rosie. Gabe and Rachel's relationship grew slowly and pain was involved considering their pasts, but in a SEP's manner, they do end up together. Ethan and Kristy were an odd pair, but I loved them too. Ethan's mind was highly fascinating, especially since he was supposed to be the pretty boy, Pastor and instead lusts over skanky women. Ethan was an ass throughout most of the book, but he was just protecting his brother. Same with Cal. He was especially cruel, but he had less emotional maturity than either of his brothers.<br /><br />The best part of this book was that everyone had flaws and bad things happen, but in the end, good things also happen. It reminds me Ain't She Sweet? without the guilty heroine needing a little redemption. Rachel just had to survive a whole lot of hate, all because of a crooked husband. I also like having children and family as part of the story. SEP wins again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="740180458926810094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_638776629" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/638776629" />
    <a title="MRB" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21024136-mrb"><img alt="MRB" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381521299p2/21024136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/638776629?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MRB" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MRB" href="/user/show/21024136-mrb">MRB</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8142670-dream-a-little-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer638776629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13083111284729161177">What a whiplash-inducing experience :) If you'd asked me to rate the first third of this book, I would have gushingly informed you that five stars just didn't feel sufficient to capture how much I loved it. I fell immediately and deeply in love with the writing style. I couldn't get over the beautifully, poignantly REAL depiction of these characters and their struggles. So we've got a down on her luck yet plucky, sassy heroine whose resourcefulness and resilient spirit enables her (and, in this </span>
  <span id="freeText13083111284729161177" style="display:none">What a whiplash-inducing experience :) If you'd asked me to rate the first third of this book, I would have gushingly informed you that five stars just didn't feel sufficient to capture how much I loved it. I fell immediately and deeply in love with the writing style. I couldn't get over the beautifully, poignantly REAL depiction of these characters and their struggles. So we've got a down on her luck yet plucky, sassy heroine whose resourcefulness and resilient spirit enables her (and, in this case, her son) to survive. And we've got a very broken hero who's drowning in pain over a tragic loss and has withdrawn from the world prior to meeting our heroine. Sounds like the setup of a mere 12 zillion other romance novels, right?! But what set this apart for me is that the author writes with an almost achingly sharp realism about the pain our heroine Rachel and, to a somewhat lesser extent, Gabe (I'm loath to call him a "hero" for reasons I'll delve into later!) are enduring. We don't just get a few hastily scribbled lines about Rachel's current poverty and hunger: we actually experience it right along with Rachel and her solemn son Edward. It takes a little longer to figure out why Gabe is such an assh---er, struggling so mightily, but once we learn of the tragedy he's suffered we can feel the sense of intolerable loss and hopelessness right along with him. Rest assured, though, that the angst is mercifully mitigated by plenty of wit and glimmers of hope. That first third or so was all so eminently engaging and effective and amusing and beautifully sad---a book that was wholly in my heart rather than just my head. <br /><br />And then the rest of the book happened. <br /><br />So I will readily admit that I'm not as enamored with (or tolerant of!) extreme alphas as most, which probably explains why many readers liked Gabe a whole lot more than I did. Scarily angry, icy, snarling jerks just aren't a romantic ideal for me. (And apparently this guy is actually among SEP's LESS awful heroes?! Good lord!) I realize that much of Gabe's jackassery can be attributed to the terrible tragedy he suffered. I get that, and to a large extent I even sympathize with that, but that doesn't mean I enjoyed being in this man's company for 380 pages. There's a dangerously thin line with these very damaged, drowning-in-ManPain-and-taking-it-out-on-the-world alphas between a good man who acts badly and a man who just becomes too awful for me to like and root for on any level. For a while I had complete confidence that SEP would tread that line successfully and manage to redeem Gabe in a wholly convincing way. After all, Gabe does occasionally do generous things despite acting like a jerk, right? And we're told many times that he USED to be a gentle, caring man. And he does care about our heroine---or, well, at least cares enough to make sure she doesn't literally starve to death (he buys her a few burgers from McDonald's...and, wow, even some fries!) and about having sex with her. ("I feel like a horny teenager" is about as close as our "hero" gets to expressing affection for the majority of the book.)<br /><br />But here's the dealbreaker for me: this guy is persistently and frequently AWFUL to Rachel's sickly and sad five-year-old son. Not just once or twice, but throughout nearly the whole novel. Now, I'm not one of these people who gets excessively gooey over kids, and in fact sometimes I avoid books where kids play a large role because they can be kind of precocious, cutesy and annoying for me to read about. But, wow, Gabe ranged from callous to outright cruel to Edward...who, let me reiterate, is a sad and sickly kid who's been through horrendous ordeals and is just FIVE freaking years old! We're meant to excuse this because of what Gabe has gone through, but get this: when Gabe talks about needing to "toughen up" and make a man out of this poor kid (and apparently that's accomplished by being a callous bastard), we're supposed to think he has a somewhat valid point! I did mention this kid is only FIVE and has endured an enormous amount of pain in his own young life, right?! (Extreme poverty and homelessness, the death of his father, loneliness and isolation and, oh yeah, near fatal pneumonia.) <br /><br />Rachel, an otherwise great mom, knows that Gabe is horribly unfeeling (at best) and sometimes even outright mean towards her little boy. She hates it and wants to stop sleeping with Gabe and all that, and then...stays with him anyway. And this is for a guy she's known for a very short period of time who's already announced he doesn't love her, can't be in a bona fide relationship and won't get past his own very serious demons, by the way. Whatever. Oh, and Gabe and Edward spend about a page reconciling towards the end and we're supposed to think it's all okay, but honestly, I was somewhat alarmed to think that after treating him so shabbily for nearly the whole novel this dark, "demon-plagued" man would be helping to raise Edward from now on. <br /><br />And, see, this is where I was uncomfortably reminded of why I usually prefer historicals: there are just certain gender expectations and behaviors that are far more palatable to me when they take place in the 19th century than in the 2000s, and extreme "alpha-ness" in particular is easier for me to tolerate. <br /><br />Anyway, so Gabe hates poor little Edward, and Edward (quite understandably, in my book) hates Gabe, and pretty much 98% of the town hates Rachel, and both of Gabe's brothers (Ethan and Cal) hate Rachel, and Rachel hates Ethan, and Rachel and Gabe have sex but act like they semi-hate each other for portions of the novel as well...and, honestly, it's just exhausting and unpleasant. By the end, I neither bought that everyone's now living in harmony nor still liked most of these people enough to care. <br /><br />All that said, I'll probably try another book by this author. Yes, I must be a masochist ;) I really love HOW she writes despite my complaints about some of WHAT she writes, and it's so sadly rare for me to find a contemporary romance writer whose style I love. I did love her wit, her insights, and her ability to elicit such a wide variety of emotions from me (including profound annoyance, but still!) But while I neither want nor expect my heroes to be flawless (far from it!), I am at a stage in my reading where I'd like them to be...well...just a little less egregiously awful ;) <br /><br />Thanks for reading this insanely long review, and if anyone can suggest a witty, sharp SEP book with a more likable hero, please let me know! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13083111284729161177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24665574-nmmomof4?shelf=famous-wealthy-popular">famous-wealthy-popular</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24665574-nmmomof4?shelf=safe-with-exception">safe-with-exception</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2474040631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2035916844512134304"><b> 3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Overall Opinion: </b> I love stories with kids in them! I also like the occasional grieving widow/widower story as well. So, this was right up my alley! I did enjoy it, but I didn't love it. I guess I never got over Gabe's treatment and issues with Edward. I got that he would struggle with Edward because of his grief, but his actual hatred for him never fared well with me. I also didn't like how that was all resolved. I didn't feel like it was all that believable, and it was as if a switch</span>
  <span id="freeText2035916844512134304" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Overall Opinion: </b> I love stories with kids in them! I also like the occasional grieving widow/widower story as well. So, this was right up my alley! I did enjoy it, but I didn't love it. I guess I never got over Gabe's treatment and issues with Edward. I got that he would struggle with Edward because of his grief, but his actual hatred for him never fared well with me. I also didn't like how that was all resolved. I didn't feel like it was all that believable, and it was as if a switch was flipped and everything was alright! I did, however, love the h! She was one tough cookie! I also appreciated that she was simply a genuinely good person. Edward was also a great character and he broke my heart a few times with his easy acceptance. Overall it was an enjoyable read, but not going on my favorites shelf like I had hoped.<br /><br /><b>Brief Summary of the Storyline: </b> This is Rachel and Gabe's story. Rachel has been rolling with life's blows and finds herself stranded in front of Gabe's shabby drive-in theater with her young son, Edward. It takes a while, but she works her way to get the grumpy Gabe to hire her to help fix up the place. Gabe soon learns that Rachel is the infamous Widow Snopes of the con-man faith healer that died after stealing money from many people from the town, and nobody is happy about her return. Gabe had been immersing himself in the drive-in to help with his grieving of his wife and son that he lost to a car accident. Rachel and Gabe find healing powers in each other and they fall in love. There are some funny moments, some suspenseful scenes, and some sexy times...and they get a HEA ending.<br /><br /><b>POV:</b> This alternated between focusing mainly on Rachel and Gabe in 3rd person narrative. There was a side love story going on where it focused in Gabe's brother, Ethan, and Kristy as well.<br /><br /><b>Overall Pace of Story: </b> Good. I never skimmed and I thought it flowed well.<br /><br /><b>Instalove:</b> No, they take a while to develop stronger feelings.<br /><br /><b>H rating:</b> 3 stars. Gabe. I struggled with him at times, but I still understood that he was a good man underneath all his gruff exterior.<br /><br /><b>h rating:</b> 5 stars. Rachel. She had some hard times for sure! I admired her strength and how she cared about others regardless of those hard times.<br /><br /><b>Sadness level: </b>Low/moderate. I teared up a few times, but I never needed any tissues.<br /><br /><b>Push/Pull:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They both have moments of pushing away (H more so at the beginning and h more so at the end) and they both also pursue the relationship at times.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Heat level:</b> Good. They have some good tension, chemistry, and scenes -- but not so much it takes away from the story.<br /><br /><b>Descriptive sex:</b> Yes<br /><br /><b>OW/OM drama:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The H does have some moments of feeling guilt over his dead wife and his moving on with the h. The h does feel at times that she can't compete with his dead wife.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Sex scene with OW or OM:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Cheating: </b> No<br /><br /><b>Separation:</b> Not really. Once they are together they stay together. <br /><br /><b>Possible Triggers: </b>Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Loss of a spouse (h off page), loss of a spouse and child (H off page), extreme poverty (h on page), and child kidnapping (on page). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Closure: </b> This had a cute ending with some good closure and what I would call a HEA ending.<br /><br /><b>Safety:</b> This one should be either <u>Safe</u> or <u>Safe with exception</u> for most safety gang readers depending on personal preferences.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have cheating<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a descriptive sex scene with OW/OM<br />- <b> Does</b> have both the h and H pushing away<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have a separation between the h and H<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have abuse<br />- <b>Does </b> have a HEA ending <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer760516277957226281"><b>Re-read</b><br/>This is probably one of my favorites of SEP as it has all the quirky humor and wry banter without the sometimes questionable practices that occur in some of her books: no-one pretends to be an underage teen in a sex game, or a gigolo, no stolen pregnancies via false birth control or sleep drugs, and no raping of the alpha men by their soon to be heroines. <br/><br/>The heroine and hero have a humorous and tough redemption, but it works for both of them. One thing that really worked is that despite </span>
  <span id="freeText760516277957226281" style="display:none"><b>Re-read</b><br />This is probably one of my favorites of SEP as it has all the quirky humor and wry banter without the sometimes questionable practices that occur in some of her books: no-one pretends to be an underage teen in a sex game, or a gigolo, no stolen pregnancies via false birth control or sleep drugs, and no raping of the alpha men by their soon to be heroines. <br /><br />The heroine and hero have a humorous and tough redemption, but it works for both of them. One thing that really worked is that despite the horror the hero has been though, Rachel doesn't treat his tragedy with kid gloves. She says his wife and child's are and doesn't make allowances. All of which helps his healing.<br /><br />There's a sweet touch of mystical grace that is nice as well. <br /><br /><b>First review</b><br />I am on a binge of Susan Elizabeth Phillips from quite a long time ago. This is one of her better books from the Chicago Stars series.<br /><br />Rachel Stone is the despised widow (Tammy Faye Baker-is) of an evangelist that stole and stole and stole then blamed it all on his wife’s materialism. Unfortunately, he is dead now, and the buck stops with her. She’s on her way back to Salvation, NC to find some of the money he left behind. One, she has debts she has to pay, and, two, she has her 5 year old little boy to consider. <br /><br />Dirt poor, her car dies next to a rundown drive-in theater that the hero is renovating. <br /><br />Gabe, brother to the H in Nobody’s Baby but Mine, is widower who lost both wife and child and is bullet away from committing suicide.<br /><br />A good story of redemption for both characters with plenty of snark and banter between the H and h. The secondary characters are well done as well. Smaller side plots include the sad tension between the H and the heroine’s 5 year old son, and the H’s other brother, a preacher that is having a hard time adjusting to his secretary’s new sexy look.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A_Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A_Ryan" href="/user/show/23384676-a-ryan">A_Ryan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=awesome-5-stars-2016-17">awesome-5-stars-2016-17</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=100-book-reading-challenge-2016">100-book-reading-challenge-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=the-cover-is-a-lie-lie-lie">the-cover-is-a-lie-lie-lie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=awesome-heroine">awesome-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=danger-or-hurt">danger-or-hurt</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720811939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10757256218446241964"><b> 5 STARS </b><br/><br/>Another 5-star read from Susan Elizabeth Phillips!! <br/><br/>I absolutely LOVE this series...<br/><br/><b> Best Bits: </b> There is so much to love about this 4th instalment of the Chicago Stars series. For me, the depth and integrity of the characters was the real winner here. My heart bled for Rachel, Gabe and Edward and I lapped up the indulgent sweetness of Ethan and Kristy as well (their story was a lot more predictable... but no less enjoyable.)<br/><br/>It's like an awesome bonus! Two love stories for the price of </span>
  <span id="freeText10757256218446241964" style="display:none"><b> 5 STARS </b><br /><br />Another 5-star read from Susan Elizabeth Phillips!! <br /><br />I absolutely LOVE this series...<br /><br /><b> Best Bits: </b> There is so much to love about this 4th instalment of the Chicago Stars series. For me, the depth and integrity of the characters was the real winner here. My heart bled for Rachel, Gabe and Edward and I lapped up the indulgent sweetness of Ethan and Kristy as well (their story was a lot more predictable... but no less enjoyable.)<br /><br />It's like an awesome bonus! Two love stories for the price of one!! And I loved both equally: Gabe and Rachel are the two tragic souls, each with heartbreaking pasts, who don't get along AT ALL in the beginning, but also find strength in the raw honesty of their dynamic. And then there's Ethan and Kristy, friends since childhood who learn to find their true potential as adults.<br /><br />I also really enjoyed the spiritual/religious thread throughout this book, something I haven't come across that often. It would have been so easy for SEP to preach to her readers and ruin the narrative with campy stereotypes. Instead, she took the road less travelled and showed how faith and religion can be abused, misunderstood, manipulated, and embraced by people with both good and bad intentions. I was particularly intrigued by Rachel's journey in this respect, and loved what she represented.<br /><br />The final reveal about Rachel provided another layer to her relationship with Gabe as well, and provided me with a deeper understanding about the effect she had on him. It all fell into place. It was the last piece of the puzzle... and I didn't see it coming at all.<br /><br />Phillips writes with a masterful hand.... it's editted beautifully, the story develops unexpectedly, and the imagery of Annie's cabin is just as powerful as it was in book 3. <br /><br /><b> The Worst Bit </b> The cover!!! This cover is all wrong for this book!!! What the hell are the flowers and sundresses doing on the cover of this book??? The main character spends the whole book wearing men's shoes and tattered hand me down clothes and wild hair... NOTHING LIKE THE COVER. The story is heartbreaking and intense and shrouded in preconceptions and small-mind judgement so why are there pretty flower graphics on the cover?? <br /><br /><b> Recommended for: </b> Lovers of well-written, well-developed characters who overcome adversity and find strength in one another. Lovers of drama mixed with comedy, good dialogue an strong, kick-arse heroines! This is a must-read!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10757256218446241964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7342077515126650243">5++ stars!<br/><br/>Another terrific installment in this outstanding series. This book was soooo goooood! Loved it. Once again SEP surprised me big time.I still feel bad because I had not read anything from this author before, I adore her style so much now.<br/><br/>Do you know what's so good about this series? It's the way the author makes it seem so real. I'm usually a paranormal-romance reader so I don't care much about contemporary romance. I don't like cheesy or corny stories. So that's what's so good about th</span>
  <span id="freeText7342077515126650243" style="display:none">5++ stars!<br /><br />Another terrific installment in this outstanding series. This book was soooo goooood! Loved it. Once again SEP surprised me big time.I still feel bad because I had not read anything from this author before, I adore her style so much now.<br /><br />Do you know what's so good about this series? It's the way the author makes it seem so real. I'm usually a paranormal-romance reader so I don't care much about contemporary romance. I don't like cheesy or corny stories. So that's what's so good about this series. I cry, laugh and bite my nails hard so many times I stopped counting them. I couldn't put it down. I know many have given 3 stars to the books in this series and I just don't understand it. The romance is so good and real, but more important the plot is always amazing.<br /><br />In this installment we have a single mother arriving to her home town after suffering many injustices. Of course she is lucky enough to come into Gabe's way. Oh you, lucky lucky girl,lol. I loved Gabe. He was given a family with an amazing and caring wife and a very cute boy just to loose them against a drunk driver. He was a man suffering, almost loosing himself into pain. But with the help of the heroine some time after he finds a way to survive and put his life together. They face many problems and uncomfortable situations, and at the end everything works out just perfectly.<br /><br />I love this author, I like her style a lot and definitely recommend it, so please if you read this series let me know, I would love to talk about it. It is driving me crazy, in a good way,LOL.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17389437259753293765"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511817724i/24546462._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>***FIVE STARS***</b><br/>My lovely friend Anna recommended this baby to me <br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Thank you for that Sweet Anna <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511818712ra/24546560.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, <br/>and I couldn't have loved it more. I'm a sucker for angsty stories, and this one had it in spades. Poor Rachel was treated horrifically by an entire town for crimes she was unjustly blamed for. Destitute and emaciated, she couldn't get ahead, or get forgiveness from almost anybody in the entire town. Rachel never lost her strength, her pride, or her wit, and her prot</span>
  <span id="freeText17389437259753293765" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511817724i/24546462._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>***FIVE STARS***</b><br>My lovely friend Anna recommended this baby to me <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Thank you for that Sweet Anna <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511818712ra/24546560.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, <br>and I couldn't have loved it more. I'm a sucker for angsty stories, and this one had it in spades. Poor Rachel was treated horrifically by an entire town for crimes she was unjustly blamed for. Destitute and emaciated, she couldn't get ahead, or get forgiveness from almost anybody in the entire town. Rachel never lost her strength, her pride, or her wit, and her protectiveness over her boy showed her true character and nature. Gabe was truly a douche to Rachel in the beginning of this story, and his brothers were over the top obnoxious assholes to her, never cutting Rachel any slack. This story was golden. I'm not giving anything else about it away, other than to say it is an extremely satisfying read and left me so happy. I loved every second of it and was truly sad when I finished it. I totally recommend this baby. <br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_344246694" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344246694" />
    <a title="F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5469257-f"><img alt="F" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367179924p2/5469257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344246694?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="F" href="/user/show/5469257-f">F</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344246694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11589718794213508376">Downtrodden and desperate, Rachel Stone returns to the town of her youth (whose residents her deceased TV evangelical husband conned and all but bankrupted) to find a lost 5 million dollars to raise her five year old son, Edward. <br/><br/>The secondary plot line is just as ridiculous and insulting. Reverend Ethan Bonner (let’s not even discuss that the man hears the voice of God as three different celebs in his head) is as hypocritical as the lambasted TV evangelical, Dwayne. Attracted to scantily clad a</span>
  <span id="freeText11589718794213508376" style="display:none">Downtrodden and desperate, Rachel Stone returns to the town of her youth (whose residents her deceased TV evangelical husband conned and all but bankrupted) to find a lost 5 million dollars to raise her five year old son, Edward. <br /><br />The secondary plot line is just as ridiculous and insulting. Reverend Ethan Bonner (let’s not even discuss that the man hears the voice of God as three different celebs in his head) is as hypocritical as the lambasted TV evangelical, Dwayne. Attracted to scantily clad and sexually available women, the Rev’ Bonner pays little attention to his doting and dowdy secretary, who does all but help him dress, until she changes her style into that of a “really stylish tramp.” Then, of course, she is a “slut”; but, a slut who has his attention. <br /><br />Dream a Little Dream has heavy Christian tones throughout the book, although this had little no affect on my enjoyment (or lack thereof) of the novel it should be noted that it can be a little too heavy at times and the novel would perhaps appeal more to those readers who do have a Christian background.<br /><br />I had heard good things of Susan Elizabeth Phillips and cannot help but be, not only disappointed, but shocked and slightly horrified at her tale. Her controlling, misogynistic, hypocritical - but hey at least they’re good looking and great in the sack! - heroes are unsympathetic, unattractive and, quite frankly, repellent. Her female characters are weak in characterisation; more flawed then they are admirable; and in desperate need of a psychiatrist. While the plot-line is fairly standard and predictable, execution leaves much to be desired (Phillips’s epilogue reads like a child’s essay) and, although I know that I probably should, I am unsure whether I wish to read another of her novels. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11589718794213508376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Stewart" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart">Jane Stewart</a>
      </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123818165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12870778634083987200">Mostly sad until the end. But the ending was nice.<br/><br/>I’ve given 5 stars to many of S E Phillips’ books, but this book gets 4 stars because it was too sad. Most of the sadness was grieving for dead loved ones and being treated badly by others. I generally prefer uplifting or funny stories. Gabe wanted to kill himself and had a hard time after his wife and son were killed by a drunk driver. Rachel was married to an unethical tv evangelist. He convinced people to give him money that he used to enrich </span>
  <span id="freeText12870778634083987200" style="display:none">Mostly sad until the end. But the ending was nice.<br /><br />I’ve given 5 stars to many of S E Phillips’ books, but this book gets 4 stars because it was too sad. Most of the sadness was grieving for dead loved ones and being treated badly by others. I generally prefer uplifting or funny stories. Gabe wanted to kill himself and had a hard time after his wife and son were killed by a drunk driver. Rachel was married to an unethical tv evangelist. He convinced people to give him money that he used to enrich himself. He died in a plane crash and the public hated Rachel, thinking she was his partner, but she too had been taken advantage of. She lives in poverty, with her 5 yr old son.<br /><br />I read the paperback twice and recently listened to the audiobook. I liked it better the second and third time since I was prepared for the sadness. I could better appreciate how Rachel reacted defiantly to her circumstances which nudged Gabe. For example page 194 “She smiled again, and pleasure leached into some of the barren places inside him. He thought about how she managed to find amusement in the smallest things, even with her life hanging in shreds around her.”<br /><br />I loved Rachel's smartness, witty comments and actions in the face of poverty and ill treatment by others. I enjoyed the secondary story about Kristy and Ethan.<br /><br />I think Susan Elizabeth Phillips is a wonderful writer. One of the reasons is character creation. I’m reminded of Sol Stein's advice to writers: “Imbue your heroes with faults and your villains with charm.” The characters in this story are a good example. Rachel is homeless, no money, no job, and caring for her son. Ethan is a minister who refuses to help her. Gabe is a recluse due to grief. He is hostile and mean to Rachel and tells her to go away. When the cops start to arrest her for vagrancy, Gabe is the only one to come to her rescue and finds her a place to live and gives her a job.<br /><br />AUDIOBOOK NARRATOR:<br />Anna Fields was excellent.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Narrative mode: 3rd person. Story length: 390 pages. Swearing language: strong including religious swear words but rarely used. Sexual language: mild. Number of sex scenes: 6. Setting: current day Salvation, North Carolina. Copyright: 1998. Genre: contemporary romance.<br /><br />OTHER BOOKS:<br />For a list of my reviews of other Susan Elizabeth Phillips books, see my 5 star review of “It Had To Be You.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="12870778634083987200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Holly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7383561-holly"><img alt="Holly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374678939p2/7383561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8142670-dream-a-little-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7383561-holly?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7383561-holly?shelf=favorite-book">favorite-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7383561-holly?shelf=cute-kid">cute-kid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7383561-holly?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1807464099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12559343589250501770">4.5 stars<br/>Some romance books are great to read but usually they don’t make much of an emotional impact because they are just so far removed from your own life experiences. So maybe it's just because I also have a 5 year-old son like the heroine, but this book absolutely struck a chord with me (even though I don't have anything else in common with the heroine). <br/><br/>This is a really heartrending story about a single mother named Rachel who is more than down on her luck and is ostracized by the entire c</span>
  <span id="freeText12559343589250501770" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br />Some romance books are great to read but usually they don’t make much of an emotional impact because they are just so far removed from your own life experiences. So maybe it's just because I also have a 5 year-old son like the heroine, but this book absolutely struck a chord with me (even though I don't have anything else in common with the heroine). <br /><br />This is a really heartrending story about a single mother named Rachel who is more than down on her luck and is ostracized by the entire community for something she can reasonably be blamed for by others. It's also about Gabe’s struggles with an unimaginable loss in his past and his attempts to bury his pain through distraction and anger. When these two characters meet for the first time it’s hard to imagine making a worse first impression. Seeing their distaste and distrust slowly transform into desire and devotion is riveting. There’s also a surprising side-plot between two secondary characters, Gabe’s brother Ethan and Ethan’s longtime friend Kristy. All of these characters are so painfully real and their struggles are hard to witness at times because they’re so ugly, but it absolutely makes for a captivating story. <br /><br />In case it interests you or bothers you, I feel the need to note that there are some Christian undertones to the book, though nothing too preachy, however this is definitely not a ‘clean’ romance. Oh, and this is part of a series, but it reads as a standalone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12559343589250501770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
